=100  \\$aZehentner, Paul$d1589-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q55874362$97979
=245  \\$aPromontorium malæ spei: impiis periculose navigantibus propositum
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aHaupt; Widmanstadt$bGraz$c1643
=300  \\$a[xxxviii]-752-[10] pages$bgilt edges, 2 engravings
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJesuit warning of the consequences of licentiousness ("Promontory, thoughts of hope for the wicked goal that sailed dangerously. Whether it is a sign of rejection and note: procrastination of repentance written precautionary men's amendment is reluctance, sometimes hope to repent.")
=500  \\$aFirst and only edition of a Latin edifying text on moral and religious issues by the Jesuit Paul Zehentner (1589-1648), preacher at the Graz court of the widow of the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand II and teacher of grammar, the humanities and the Holy Scripture at Millestadt in Austria. A moral-theological treatment of state theory, astrology and magic, intended to highlight the dangers of licentious behaviour. 
=500  \\$aIt provides our first known reference to the tragedy of Leontius, a play Zehentner saw at the Jesuit University in Ingolstadt in 1615, and which was to serve as a prototype for the Don Juan legend (Keefe, Mozart studies, p. 140). 
=500  \\$aZehentner dedicated the book to Leonardus Helfridus, Count at Maggau, 26 October 1643, and received a privilege from the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand III.
=500  \\$aEngraved allegorical frontispiece and a richly designed armorial and emblematic dedication plate, both by David Tscherning.
=504  \\$aindex
=590  \\$aSive, signum & nota reprobationis: procrastinatio poenitentiae, scripta cautelae hominum, emendatione[m] vita[e] cunctantium, spe aliquando resipiscendi.

=500  \\$aIn 1822 Logier was called to Berlin to help found a music academy, and subsequently trained elementary teachers on behalf of the king until 1826. In addition, the publishing house of his brother Wilhelm published his textbooks in German.  In this method, several pupils are taught at a time, with technical instruction done together with instruction in principles of harmony. This lay the basis of group teaching in music.

=500  \\$aA blind 18th century musician based in London, Starling Goodwin wrote music both for church use and public concerts. Surviving examples of his work include voluntaries for organ or harpsichord and a number of popular light entertainment songs. One of the greatest pluralists of his profession, he was organist at four London churches simultaneously at the time of his death. He was also a witty and amusing socialiser and an accomplished violinist.

=041  \\$adut$alat
=041  \\$alat
=059  \\$av
=245  \\$aMissen en gezangen
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aUtrecht$bWeyde, van der$c1745
=300  \\$a[i]-48-[2] pages
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe so-called 'Stukjesboek', which formed the basis of the old Catholic church song in the Netherlands: 98 songs in Latin and Dutch, plus three ordinaria in Latin. Strong Jansenist influence.
=500  \\$aMissen en Gezangen is not the only para-liturgical hymnbook that the Utrecht Church had after the schism of 1723.
Some of the material it contains had already been published in Het Paradijs, which appeared in eight editions between 1621 and 1679 in Antwerp, or in Het Prieel, Brugues 1609/l0. Also the collection of Gulielmus de Swaen, parish priest in Gouda, to which he gave the name Den Singende Swaen'[, -an allusion to his own name, which means 'swan', - contains pieces that can be found in Missen en Gezangen. Of a substantial part, however, the origin remains obscure. No doubt a large repertoire of Latin and Dutch hymns was known from the rather isolated milieu of the Utrecht church. It is even possible that the type of hymns found in Missen en Gezangen and the other collections mentioned, were cherished by the secular clergy and that their use was discouraged, more or less, by the regulars. It is at least curious that in the Old Catholic Church an abundance of hymns have survived, while they are relatively rare in the Roman Catholic Church parishes in Friesland and northern Holland.
=500  \\$aIn Missen en Gezangen we find texts by Andreas van der Schuur and Jean Baptiste Stalpaert van der Wielen , but most of the texts are from the Counter-Reformation period and are anonymous.
=500  \\$aAndreas van der Schuur (also Van der Schuer) (1656- 1719) was ordained a priest in 1680 and became parish priest in Vianen in 1692. Archbishop Van Neercassel entrusted him with the translation of the Bible  in 1732, completed by H. van Rhijn. He was the composer of several religious poems, both Latin and Dutch.


=500  \\$aJean Baptiste Stalpa(e)rt van der Wiele(n) (1579 - 1630), a lawyer in The Hague in 1598,  became a priest in 1606. In 1613 he was appointed parish priest in Delft, where he remained until his death. In 1621 he published "Hemelrijk", in 1622 "Het vrouwelick cieraed van St Agnes", religious poetry. In prose he published "Roomsche Reys" in 1624, and in 1628 a collection of hymns "'t
Gulden Jaer ons'Heeren Jesu Christi". As a posthumous work he published "Extractum Catholicum" and "Guide Jaers Feestdaghen of de Schat der gheestelijekeLofsanghen", in 1631 and 1634. He was the composer of about 2000 hymns.

=500  \\$asong by a female composer, a member of the Ukrainian princely family Kotschoubey. Princess Elisabeth Vassilievna Kotschoubey (née Kotschoubey) (1821-1897) was a well known composer of both Russian and French popular songs in Russia and later in France. She was  married to her third cousin, Prince Leon Viktorovitch Kotschoubey (1810-1890) and they died childless. 
=500  \\$aEnrico Tamberlik (16 March 1820 – 13 March 1889) was an Italian tenor who sang to great acclaim at Europe and America's leading opera venues. He excelled in the heroic roles of the Italian and French repertories and was renowned for his powerful declamation and clarion high notes.
=500  \\$aText writer Larmande was a French state official (chef de bureau au Ministère des Finances), and amateur poet. Known for translating German songs, or rather for providing them with new, French poetry, e.g. in the series Échos d'Allemagne, together with Victor Wilder. His official signature (e.g. on his appointment as Chevalier de la légion d'honneur in 1881) always reads "Ad. Larmande", and his brother Alfred Larmande and sister-in-law Sophie Desargues were professional musicians.
=500  \\$aErnesto Cavallini (1807-74) clarinetist and composer, created in 1862 'Trois Variations sur la romance Oh!Dites-Lui' for Clarinet and orchestra:

=100  \\$aVoormolen, Alexander$d1895-1980$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2281256$96188
=245  \\$aCecilia (Oud Nederlandsch)
=246  \1$aCecilia. Middeleeuwsch Lied
=260  \\$aNetherlands$c1922
=300  \\$a5 pages
=500  \\$aPrinted and manuscript (Autograph?) version of the same song
=500  \\$aperformer's notes and markings in pensil on the manuscript version
=500  \\$acomposition place and date marked on manuscript version "'s-Gravenhage 1922"
=500  \\$aThis love song "Ik zag Cecilia komen" about the shepherds Cecilia and Floriaan, dates back to the 17th century. The oldest entry is in the Album of Geesken ter Borch (1652), with the opening line "Siet het pluijm gevogelt". The famous line with Cecilia is only found in verse 2 of the 2nd strophe. It also appears as "Lied van Cecilia" in the 'Dordrecht Helikon, ofte De Groote Dubbele Hollandsche Nachtegael' (1719). The song has lived on in the oral tradition, perhaps partly due to the fact that it has been included in numerous collections of folk songs. The melody is vaguely found in the Ballo di Mantova (Dance from Mantua) attributed to the guitar virtuoso Francisco Corbetta (1615-1681) and in "Fuggi fuggi da questo cielo" by Giuseppino Cenci (Giuseppino di Roma).
=561  \\$aManuscript version dedicated by the composer to Birgit Engell

=245  \\$aTwee Koraalvoorspelen in Barokstijl voor orgel met pedaal:$bHoe zal ik U ontvangen/Valet will ich dir geben - O God die droeg ons voorgeslacht/O God our help in ages past

=500  \\$atranslation of Paul Gerhardt's Advent song "Wie soll ich dich empfangen"
=500  \\$a"Valet will ich dir geben" is a Lutheran hymn written by Valerius Herberger in 1613. It is a Sterbelied (hymn for the dying). The text was published with two hymn tunes by Melchior Teschner, Zahn Nos. 5403 and 5404a, in 1615. The second of these melodies was used in compositions such as chorale preludes by Johann Sebastian Bach and Max Reger. Bach used single stanzas in vocal works, including his St John Passion.
=500  \\$a"Our God, Our Help in Ages Past" is a hymn by Isaac Watts in 1708 that paraphrases the 90th Psalm of the Book of Psalms. In 1738, John Wesley in his hymnal, Psalms and Hymns, changed the first line of the text from "Our God" to "O God". Both Watts' wording and Wesley's rewording remain in current use.

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aNewspaper extract of the Algemeen Handelsblad of 28 mai 1852 (an influential Amsterdam-based liberal daily newspaper published between 1828 and 1970), on the occasion of King Willem III unveiling in 1852 a cast-iron Rembrandt monument designed by Louis Royer on the Amsterdam Botermarkt-square (named Rembrandtplein since 1876). 
=500  \\$a4 pages Biography, ending with poem by Thijm, plus 2 pages text that appeared on the title page of the Newspaper.
=500  \\$aThe biography ends with a long celebrating poem on Rembrandt by J.A. Alberdingk Thijm (1820-1889) titled "Een Harptoon in het Akkoord der Rembrandtshulde"
https://www.dbnl.org/tekst/albe003voor01_01/albe003voor01_01_0016.php

=041  \\$ager
=245  \\$aUnter Allerhöchster Autoriteit Ihro Kön. Maj. zu Dännemark, Norwegen u. Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen 40stes Stück. Montag den 7ten October 1799
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1799
=300  \\$a4 pages$bquadruple-folded pages$c42x36c cm
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen (SchlHA) is the justice journal of the German federal state of Schleswig-Holstein and at the same time one of the oldest periodicals of the state.
The Schleswig-Holsteinische Anzeigen date back to the time of the duchies of Schleswig and Holstein and have been published since 1750.[1] They are an announcement journal that was published under the same title by both the kings of Denmark and the diverse rulers in Schleswig-Holstein such as the House of Schleswig-Holstein-Gottorf. Today, the publisher is the state's Ministry of Justice, which has left the editorship to the Higher Regional Court of Schleswig. They are divided into a monthly Part A (with the editorial content of a legal journal and contributions on case law in the judicial district of the state's only Higher Regional Court) and a twice-monthly Part B (advertising section and judicial notices). It is therefore an official journal and not an advertising journal.
Part B of the Schleswig-Holstein Advertisements was published twice a month (on the 15th and 30th of a month) in printed form as a justice gazette until the end of 2014. The publication of a written edition of Part B has been dispensed with since 1 January 2015. Therefore, from this date onwards, all issues of Part B (which in future will only be published once on the 30th of a month) will only be made available digitally and free of charge.

=100  \\$aRabutin, Roger de$d1618-1693$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q733246$98816
=245  \\$aLettres de Messire Roger de Rabutin, Comte de Bussy ... avec les réponses $n1-3,5,6/6
=250  \\$a2nd ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bChatelain$c1752
=300  \\$a5 vols. ([xix]-360+[x]-374+[xii]-390+[xii]-375+[x]-358 pages)$bmarbled edges, leather bound, gild embossed spine, marbled endpapers, engraved title page, title page in red and black ink
=500  \\$aRoger de Rabutin, comte de Bussy, commonly known as Bussy-Rabutin, was a French memoirist, a lieutenant-general in the armies of King Louis XIV, a courtier at the French court, a philosopher and epistolary writer, a pamphleteer, a satirist and a libertine, and a member of the Académie française. He was the cousin and frequent correspondent of Madame de Sévigné.
=500  \\$aFrontispiece vol.1 contains beautiful portrait engraving of the author

=500  \\$aoriginates from a Benectine monastery school ?
=500  \\$aEx libris "Dom Antoine Jourdez", the last Benedictine monk of Toul, who wrote a handwritten document, entitled Description of the organ, 1811 and 1813. Attached to this 422-page manuscript is a 47-page Supplement, written in 1882, by Joseph Oury, organist of Toul Cathedral. The organ of the former Saint-Étienne Cathedral of Toul (Meurthe-et-Moselle) seemed to have passed through the Revolution without incident. When the church reopened, the last of the Benedictine monks of Saint-Mansuy, Dom Antoine Jourdez, had the organ restored and assumed the position of organist until September 30, 1828.

=100  \\$aEkkart, Rudolf E. O.$4aut$910709
=245  10$aLief & leed:$brealisme en fantasie in Nederlandse familiegroepen uit de zeventiende en achttiende eeuw
=246  3\$aLief en leed
=264  \1$aZwolle:$bWaanders$aEnschede$bRijksmuseum Twenthe$c2018
=300  \\$a208 pages :$billustrations (chiefly color), portraits ;$c27 cm
=336  \\$atext$btxt$2rdacontent
=336  \\$astill image$bsti$2rdacontent
=337  \\$aunmediated$bn$2rdamedia
=338  \\$avolume$bnc$2rdacarrier
=504  \\$aIncludes bibliographical references (pages 198-202) and index.
=505  0\$aInleiding -- Families in beeld: de ontwikkeling van de familiegroep vanaf de zestiende eeuw -- Realisme en fantasie: Nederlandse familiegroepen en andere portretten -- De herkenbare dood: overleden gezinsleden in het familieportret -- De vermomde dood: schijnbaar levende gezinsleden in het familieportret -- Gezinsuitbreiding: bijgeschilderde familieleden -- Slotwoord.
=520  8\$a"Familieportretten uit de Gouden Eeuw, maar ook later, verbeelden de schone schijn. Op het eerste gezicht lijken zij realistisch, maar dat blijkt lang niet altijd het geval. Op verzoek van hun opdrachtgevers maakten portretschilders uit de 17de en 18de eeuw zich geregeld schuldig aan 'beeldmanipulatie'. Overleden personen zijn als levend afgebeeld en met een huwelijk of geboorte werden nieuwe familieleden bijgeschilderd. Na een flinke ruzie werden figuren net zo makkelijk ook weer gewist uit de voorstelling. Met een kritische blik en jaren van onderzoek laten de auteurs zien dat zelfs in de portretkunst, het ogenschijnlijk meest waarheidsgetrouwe genre in de beeldende kunst, de waarheid niet altijd even nauw wordt genomen. De mooiste verhalen komen aan het licht. Verhalen over perfecte huwelijken en verboden liefdes. Over de plotselinge dood en de vreugde van nieuw leven. Over het lief en leed van het familiebestaan"--$cPublisher's website.

=100  \\$aJas, Eric$4aut$911853
=245  13$aDe Leidse koorboeken:$been ongehoorde schat
=260  \\$aZoetermeer$bBoekencentrum$c2011
=300  \\$a88 p. :$bill., music ;$c25 cm.
=520  8\$aVan de honderden koorboeken die Nederland in de zestiende eeuw rijk was, is slechts een dertiental bewaard gebleven. Zes van deze enorme, prachtige en handgeschreven boeken - een unieke, kostbare muziekschat - werden speciaal gemaakt voor het koor van de Leidse Pieterskerk, dat daar dagelijks de zeven getijden uit zong. Tot aan de Reformatie. Toen verdwenen ze voor eeuwen in een kist. Dit rijk geïllustreerde boekje vertelt het verhaal van de Leidse Koorboeken. Het leest als een spannende novelle, waarin naast de boeken ook deftige families, kleurrijke componisten, grafgangen, de handel in jongenssopranen, luie zangers en beeldenstormers een belangrijke rol spelen.

=500  \\$aWerner Wolffheim was a German lawyer and musicologist with a majorly important music collection. The auction sale of his library in 1928 and 1929 was an important event in the world of (early) music, musicology, and book collectors. A large part of the collection was bought by Paul Hirsch.

=500  \\$aAmédée Reuchsel was a French composer and organist. He studied music at the Conservatories of Brussels and Paris; in the latter he had as teacher in composition the master Gabriel Fauré. He obtained the position of organist of the church of Saint Dionysus in Paris and in 1908 he was awarded the Chartier prize for chamber music. His father Léon (1840-1915) was also a musician, as were his brother Maurice (1880-1968) and his son Eugène (1900-1988).

=100  \\$aHaydn, Joseph$d1732-1809$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7349$94783

=300  \\$a[i]-4-[ii]-100-[i]- pages$balternating pages of text and music, Vols. 1, 3 and 4 in a blue custom made case, engraved ill. as frontispiece.
=500  \\$a"A Select Collection of Original Scottish Airs for the Voice" is a multi-volume collection of Scottish song edited and published by the entrepreneurial musician, publisher and Clerk to the Board of Trustees for Encouragement of Art and Manufacture in Scotland, George Thomson. For the first volume, which appeared in 1793, Thomson commissioned the composer Ignaz Pleyel to provide musical settings.

From the Preface of Vol. 3: "For the composition of these [the symphonies and accompaniments], he entered into terms with Mr Pleyel, who fulfilled part of his engagement very satisfactorily; but having then deserted it, the Editor, after a fruitless correspondence with him, which retarded the progress of the Work for years, at length found it necessary to turn his eyes elsewhere. He was so fortunate, however, [...] as to engage Mr Kozeluch and Dr Haydn, to proceed with the Work, which they have finished in such a manner, as to leave him without any other regret, but that of having so long delayed his application to them." 

This is the second edition of the first volume, published in 1803, in which Thomson has replaced 21 of the previously published version with settings by Haydn.  
=500  \\$aContains a full page engraved illustration "The Birks of Invermay Soldier's Return".
=500  \\$aWith Thomson's signature on title page.
=501  \\$aIn a case with Vols. 3 and 4 of the same collection. See also G2-001.
=590  \\$aWith Introductory & Concluding Symphonies & Accompaniments for the Piano Forte, Violin & Violoncello by Pleyel, Kozeluch & Haydn. With Select & Characteristic Verses both Scottish and English adapted to the Airs, including upwards of One Hundred New Songs by Burns.

For the first volume, which appeared in 1793, Thomson commissioned the composer Ignaz Pleyel to provide musical settings.

He was so fortunate, however, [...] as to engage Mr Kozeluch and Dr Haydn, to proceed with the Work, which they have finished in such a manner, as to leave him without any other regret, but that of having so long delayed his application to them."
